	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Newcastle railway station</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Mainline railway station in Newcastle upon Tyne, England</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Newcastle Central" redirects here. For the parliamentary constituency, see <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne_Central_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Newcastle upon Tyne Central (UK Parliament constituency)">Newcastle upon Tyne Central (UK Parliament constituency)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the main line station in Newcastle-upon-Tyne. For the Tyne &amp; Wear Metro station, see <a href="/wiki/Central_Station_Metro_station" title="Central Station Metro station">Central Station Metro station</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Newcastle railway station (disambiguation)">Newcastle railway station (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Newcastle railway station</b> (also known as <b>Newcastle Central Station</b>) is on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> in the United Kingdom, serving the city of <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle upon Tyne</a>, Tyne and Wear. It is 268.633 miles (432.323&#160;km) down the line from <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King's Cross</a><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and on the main line it is situated between <a href="/wiki/Chester-le-Street_railway_station" title="Chester-le-Street railway station">Chester-le-Street</a> to the south and <a href="/wiki/Manors_railway_station" title="Manors railway station">Manors</a> to the north. Its three-letter station code is NCL.
</p><p>Opened in 1850, it is a Grade I <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed building</a><sup id="cite_ref-Listing_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Listing-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and is located in the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_City_Centre" title="Newcastle City Centre">city centre</a> at the southern edge of <a href="/wiki/Grainger_Town" title="Grainger Town">Grainger Town</a> and to the west of the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Castle_Keep" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle Castle Keep">Castle Keep</a>. It is a nationally important transport hub, being both a terminus and through-station on the main line between London and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Durham_Coast_Line" title="Durham Coast Line">Durham Coast Line</a> to <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">Middlesbrough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nunthorpe_railway_station" title="Nunthorpe railway station">Nunthorpe</a> also the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_Valley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyne Valley Line">Tyne Valley Line</a> to <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_railway_station" title="Carlisle railway station">Carlisle</a> via <a href="/wiki/Hexham_railway_station" title="Hexham railway station">Hexham</a>. It is also served by the adjoining <a href="/wiki/Central_Station_Metro_station" title="Central Station Metro station">Central Station</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear_Metro" title="Tyne and Wear Metro">Tyne and Wear Metro</a>. As of September&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the main line station is managed by <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All London North Eastern Railway services between London and Edinburgh stop at Newcastle. <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> supplements services to Scotland, and operates trains southbound to the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West</a> and South Coast of England via Birmingham and the wider <a href="/wiki/Midlands_(England)" class="mw-redirect" title="Midlands (England)">Midlands</a> region; trains reach as far as <a href="/wiki/Penzance_railway_station" title="Penzance railway station">Penzance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Central_railway_station" title="Southampton Central railway station">Southampton Central</a>. The station is also a terminus for <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a>, which connects Newcastle to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool Lime Street</a>, via <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Victoria railway station">Manchester Victoria</a>, with some services also running to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> variously combines three routes out of Newcastle in order to provide both terminating and through services. To the west, trains connect the city to the <a href="/wiki/MetroCentre_(shopping_centre)" title="MetroCentre (shopping centre)">MetroCentre shopping centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hexham_railway_station" title="Hexham railway station">Hexham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_railway_station" title="Carlisle railway station">Carlisle</a> with intermittent extensions to <a href="/wiki/Whitehaven_railway_station" title="Whitehaven railway station">Whitehaven</a>, and north to <a href="/wiki/Morpeth_railway_station" title="Morpeth railway station">Morpeth</a> on the main line, with extensions to <a href="/wiki/Chathill_railway_station" title="Chathill railway station">Chathill</a>. To the south east, the Durham Coast Line connects to <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunderland railway station">Sunderland</a> via <a href="/wiki/Heworth_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Heworth railway station">Heworth</a> and County Durham and Teesside. Important stops include <a href="/wiki/Hartlepool_railway_station" title="Hartlepool railway station">Hartlepool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockton_railway_station_(County_Durham)" title="Stockton railway station (County Durham)">Stockton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">Middlesbrough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nunthorpe_railway_station" title="Nunthorpe railway station">Nunthorpe</a> the line is shared with the Tyne and Wear Metro to <a href="/wiki/City_of_Sunderland" title="City of Sunderland">Sunderland</a>. Additionally, Northern and <a href="/wiki/Abellio_ScotRail" title="Abellio ScotRail">Abellio ScotRail</a> jointly operate a limited service to <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow Central</a> via <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_railway_station" title="Carlisle railway station">Carlisle</a>.
</p><p>Together with the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear_Metro" title="Tyne and Wear Metro">Tyne and Wear Metro</a> and numerous local bus routes, the complex is one of the most important transport hubs in the North East. There are currently two Metro and 12 main line platforms seeing 13 million passengers annually, and in light of increasing patronage the main line station has undergone a major refurbishment to increase retail space and enhance the station environment including the controversial pedestrianisation of the portico.<sup id="cite_ref-13mill2014_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13mill2014-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <i>Britain's 100 Best Railway Stations</i> by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Jenkins" title="Simon Jenkins">Simon Jenkins</a>, the station was one of only ten to be awarded five stars.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_and_opening">Construction and opening</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Construction and opening">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conception">Conception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Conception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A scheme for a central station was proposed by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Grainger" title="Richard Grainger">Richard Grainger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Sopwith_(geologist)" title="Thomas Sopwith (geologist)">Thomas Sopwith</a> in 1836<sup id="cite_ref-grainger_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grainger-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> but was not built.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_and_Carlisle_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle and Carlisle Railway">Newcastle and Carlisle Railway</a> had agreed to relinquish their insistence on exclusively using their Redheugh terminus on the south bank of the <a href="/wiki/River_Tyne" title="River Tyne">River Tyne</a>. They agreed with <a href="/wiki/George_Hudson" title="George Hudson">George Hudson</a> on a general station north of the Tyne, near the Spital. Instead of crossing the Tyne by a low level bridge and climbing to the Spital by a rope-worked incline, they would build an extension crossing at Scotswood and approaching on the north bank. They opened this line and a temporary station at Forth, and passenger trains started using that on 1 March 1847.<sup id="cite_ref-carlisle_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carlisle-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hudson, known as the "Railway King" was concentrating on connecting his portfolio of railways so as to join Edinburgh with the English network. His Newcastle and Berwick Railway obtained its authorising Act of Parliament in 1845, but for the time being it was to use the Newcastle and North Shields Railway's station at Carliol Square. Building a crossing of the Tyne was obviously going to be a lengthy process, so that he gave the construction of the general station a low priority. The Tyne crossing became the <a href="/wiki/High_Level_Bridge" title="High Level Bridge">High Level Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fawcett_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fawcett-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-n&amp;br_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-n&amp;br-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 1846 the Newcastle and Carlisle Railway exerted pressure for the general station to be built, and the architect <a href="/wiki/John_Dobson_(architect)" title="John Dobson (architect)">John Dobson</a> was appointed by Hudson to design it, in association with the engineer <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Elliot_Harrison" title="Thomas Elliot Harrison">T E Harrison</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stephenson" title="Robert Stephenson">Robert Stephenson</a>. By now the general alignment of Hudson's railways was becoming clear: a main line from the south via Gateshead would approach over the High Level Bridge and enter the general station from the east; the Newcastle and Berwick line would be extended from Carliol Square and also enter from the east; through trains from London to Scotland would reverse in the new station. Newcastle and Carlisle Railway trains would of course enter from the west.<sup id="cite_ref-fawcett_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fawcett-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-n&amp;br_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-n&amp;br-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_definite_design">A definite design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: A definite design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_Station_(Fordyce).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Newcastle_Central_Station_%28Fordyce%29.jpg/220px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%28Fordyce%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Newcastle_Central_Station_%28Fordyce%29.jpg/330px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%28Fordyce%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Newcastle_Central_Station_%28Fordyce%29.jpg/440px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%28Fordyce%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="552" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_Station_(Fordyce).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The exterior of the station in 1867.</div></div></div>
<p>Dobson produced general plans for the station, now being referred to as the <i>Central station</i>, on a broad curve to front Neville Street so as to accommodate the alignment of the approaching railways at east and west. It was to a "Romano-Italien design with ornamental work of the Doric order".<sup id="cite_ref-bywell_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bywell-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Two through platform lines were shown, with three west end bays and two at the east end. There were to be three trainshed roofs with spans of 60 feet. Extensive offices as well as refreshment facilities were shown, and there was to be a covered carriage drive on the Neville Street side extending from the <a href="/wiki/Porte-coch%C3%A8re" title="Porte-cochère">porte-cochère</a> at each end.
</p><p>On 7 August 1847 a contract was let for the main part of the work to Mackay and Blackstock, for £92,000 (equivalent to £8,260,000&#32;in 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> A considerable amount of groundworks was necessary on the large site prior to the actual building work.<sup id="cite_ref-fawcett_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fawcett-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The work did not progress speedily, and in 1849 Hudson's collection of railway companies suffered a financial shock. At a time of more difficult trading and a tighter money market, Hudson's personal dealings were exposed as shady. The <a href="/wiki/York,_Newcastle_and_Berwick_Railway" title="York, Newcastle and Berwick Railway">York, Newcastle and Berwick Railway</a> had been formed by merger of the previous smaller companies, and the YN&amp;BR wished to reduce the financial commitment to the Central Station substantially; hotel accommodation and the covered carriage drive were eliminated. One of the through platforms was also removed from the plan.<sup id="cite_ref-fawcett_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fawcett-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As built the site covered three acres and the length of the platform faces was 830 yards.<sup id="cite_ref-bywell_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bywell-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inaugurated_by_the_Queen">Inaugurated by the Queen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Inaugurated by the Queen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_Station_(1850).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Newcastle_Central_Station_%281850%29.jpg/220px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%281850%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Newcastle_Central_Station_%281850%29.jpg/330px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%281850%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Newcastle_Central_Station_%281850%29.jpg/440px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%281850%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="982" data-file-height="539" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_Station_(1850).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The trainshed soon after opening.</div></div></div>
<p>The trainshed proved faster to construct and on 29 August 1850 Queen Victoria visited the station by train and formally opened it. The day was declared a public holiday in Newcastle.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The following day YN&amp;BR trains were diverted into it.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The trainshed was, jointly with the Lime Street station in Liverpool, the first to be designed and built in Britain using curved wrought iron ribs to support an arched roof. The large section of the ribs was fabricated using curved web plates specially rolled using bevelled rolls; the novel technique was created by Thomas Charlton of Hawks Crawshay, and was estimated to have saved 14% on the cost of the roof ironwork, compared with cutting rectilinear plates to the curve.<sup id="cite_ref-fawcett_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fawcett-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The station was lit by gas; a demonstration of electric arc-lighting was made, but was not at that date a practical possibility for the large station space. The platforms were positioned 15 inches above rail level.
</p><p>The station was shared from the beginning by the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_and_North_Shields_Railway" title="Newcastle and North Shields Railway">Newcastle and North Shields Railway</a>, which abandoned its earlier terminus at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carliol_Square_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carliol Square railway station (page does not exist)">Carliol Square</a> to the east which had operated since 1839. The <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_and_Carlisle_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle and Carlisle Railway">Newcastle and Carlisle Railway</a> started using Central station from 1 January 1851, and also abandoned its earlier terminus at Forth.<sup id="cite_ref-SRTNC_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRTNC-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1861 the York, Newcastle and Berwick Railway had already merged with others to form the <a href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Railway_(United_Kingdom)" title="North Eastern Railway (United Kingdom)">North Eastern Railway</a>, and now it was desired to amalgamate with the Newcastle and Berwick Railway too. The Corporation of Newcastle used the opportunity of the necessary Parliamentary Bill for the amalgamation to insist on construction of the abandoned porte-cochère, and this was designed by Thomas Prosser and completed in 1863.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_of_the_station">Expansion of the station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Expansion of the station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1860s the passenger train service was increasing considerably, especially as branch lines opened, six platforms were increased to nine in 1871 and to twelve in 1877, and then to fifteen in 1894: an additional through island platform was provided in 1871, occupying space formerly in use for stabling carriages. Increase in traffic continued, as also increasing train lengths and it was clear that a major extension of the station was essential. Newcastle had been given city status in 1882 and was supportive of the work, seeing it as a civic improvement. Forth Street was displaced southwards and two new trainshed roofs covered a southward extension of the station; in addition a large expansion to the east took place, with additional bay platforms there on the north side of the former bays. The original through track was blocked to form east and west bays, so that there were still only three through platform lines. This work was completed in 1894.<sup id="cite_ref-fawcett_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fawcett-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SRTNC_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRTNC-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The new group of bay platforms at the east end had their own concourse quadrangle, known at the time as the "Tynemouth Square". There was a separate booking hall for those local services. At this stage the roof covered seven and a half acres in area; there were fifteen platforms with a length of 3,000 yards.<sup id="cite_ref-bywell_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bywell-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Killingworth_Billy">Killingworth Billy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Killingworth Billy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1901 an early steam locomotive was on display at the station;&#160;:
</p>
<blockquote><p>[The station] is further graced by a pedestal on which stands a curious old locomotive rejoicing in the name of "Billy". The true early history of "Billy" is well-nigh veiled in the mists of antiquity, and it was only by diligent enquiry that Mr Holliday, the Station Master, was able to learn a little of her antecedents. That "she" was constructed as far back as 1824 – 1826 is however certain, and on that score alone she is entitled to an introduction to such of the readers of the Railway Magazine as have until now been unaware of her existence. For about fifty-five years (until 1879) she performed good service, first at the Springwell, and latterly at the Killingworth colliery, from which place she actually steamed into Newcastle in 1881 to celebrate George Stephenson’s Centenary.<sup id="cite_ref-bywell_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bywell-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>An image of the locomotive in Bywell's article is captioned "Puffing billy" but it is not <a href="/wiki/Puffing_Billy_(locomotive)" title="Puffing Billy (locomotive)">Puffing Billy</a> of 1814, which is currently on display at the Science Museum in London.
</p><p>The locomotive in Bywell's article is known simply as Billy (Built in 1826) It was presented to Newcastle upon Tyne Corporation for preservation in 1881. Initially it was displayed on a plinth at the north end of the High Level Bridge, but was moved to the interior of Newcastle Central Station in 1896; it remained there until 1945, when it was moved to the city's Museum of Science and Industry; it was moved again in 1981 to the Stephenson Railway Museum in nearby North Shields, where it is still on display.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The early history of the locomotive is uncertain; it is probably a George Stephenson locomotive, and was probably built at Killingworth Colliery workshops around 1815-1820.<sup id="cite_ref-bailey_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bailey-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_twentieth_century">The twentieth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The twentieth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:left; vertical-align:middle; padding:0 0 0 3px;"><div style="display:inline;font-size:90%;padding-left:3px">&#32;<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="font-size:90%;font-weight:inherit;color:inherit;background:transparent;margin-top:-2px;margin-bottom:-2px;display:inline-table;vertical-align:middle;text-align:inherit;"><tbody><tr><td style="text-align:inherit;padding:0;line-height:.9;font-size:105%"><a href="/wiki/Durham_Coast_Line" title="Durham Coast Line">Durham Coast Line</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:inherit;padding:0;line-height:.9;font-size:92%;font-style:italic">to <a href="/wiki/Heworth_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Heworth station">Heworth</a></td></tr></tbody></table>&#32;</div>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:right; vertical-align:middle; padding:0 3px 0 0;"><div style="display:inline;font-size:90%; padding-right:3px"></div>
</td>
<td style="padding:0; white-space:nowrap; background-color:; text-align:center !important; width:0px">
<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="background-color:transparent; float:none !important; margin:auto !important; width: auto !important; line-height: 0px !important; padding:0 !important;">

<tbody><tr>
<td class="bs-overlap" style="background-color:inherit; border:0; padding:0;"><div style="position: relative;"><a href="/wiki/File:BSicon_utCONTf.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/BSicon_utCONTf.svg/20px-BSicon_utCONTf.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/BSicon_utCONTf.svg/30px-BSicon_utCONTf.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/BSicon_utCONTf.svg/40px-BSicon_utCONTf.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a></div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:left; vertical-align:middle; padding:0 0 0 3px;"><div style="display:inline;font-size:90%;padding-left:3px">&#32;<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="font-size:90%;font-weight:inherit;color:inherit;background:transparent;margin-top:-2px;margin-bottom:-2px;display:inline-table;vertical-align:middle;text-align:inherit;"><tbody><tr><td style="text-align:inherit;padding:0;line-height:.9;font-size:105%">Tyne and Wear Metro</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:inherit;padding:0;line-height:.9;font-size:92%;font-style:italic">to <a href="/wiki/Gateshead_Stadium_Metro_station" title="Gateshead Stadium Metro station">Gateshead Stadium</a></td></tr></tbody></table>&#32;</div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td></tr>










</tbody></table>
<p>In 1900 the North Eastern Railway started replacing the gas lighting in the station with electric arc equipment. Further use of electricity came from 1904 when several suburban lines were electrified using the <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">third rail</a> system, to form the <a href="/wiki/Tyneside_Electrics" title="Tyneside Electrics">Tyneside Electrics</a> system, electric trains were introduced, using Central Station from 1 July 1904. The tracks on platforms 1 to 6 were equipped with electrified third rails, and platform 7 was later electrified to handle electric trains to <a href="/wiki/South_Shields_railway_station" title="South Shields railway station">South Shields</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SRTNC_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRTNC-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another major development came on 1 October 1906 when the <a href="/wiki/King_Edward_VII_Bridge" title="King Edward VII Bridge">King Edward VII Bridge</a> was opened, crossing the Tyne to the south-west of the station: Since 1850 <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> trains had entered Newcastle from the south via the <a href="/wiki/High_Level_Bridge" title="High Level Bridge">High Level Bridge</a> to the south-east, this meant however that they had to reverse in order to continue their journey, which lengthened journey times and led to congestion at the busy junction east of the station. The four-track King Edward Bridge remedied this by allowing north-south trains to leave or enter from either side of the station. The triangular junction at the Gateshead side also allowed for greater flexibility, allowing trains from <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunderland railway station">Sunderland</a> to use the new bridge if necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-SRTNC_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRTNC-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1909, Central station became Newcastle's only major city-centre station when the former <a href="/wiki/Blyth_and_Tyne_Railway" title="Blyth and Tyne Railway">Blyth and Tyne Railway</a>'s terminus at <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_New_Bridge_Street_railway_station" title="Newcastle New Bridge Street railway station">Newcastle New Bridge Street</a> was closed, and its trains diverted to Central station via a new connection to <a href="/wiki/Manors_railway_station" title="Manors railway station">Manors</a> station.<sup id="cite_ref-SRTNC_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRTNC-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro_station">Metro station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Metro station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear_Metro" title="Tyne and Wear Metro">Tyne and Wear Metro</a> system opened in 1980, taking over and improving many of the Tyneside suburban routes that had declined under British Railways management. The underground <a href="/wiki/Central_Station_Metro_station" title="Central Station Metro station">Central Station</a> for Metro trains was constructed during the late 1970s underneath the main line station, and opened in 1981. Part of the porte-cochère was temporarily dismantled while excavation work took place.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>  
The Metro system was a considerable success; Many conventional rail services were transferred there, and several of the east end bays were closed and converted to car parking and other usage. The Carlisle line was diverted to enter Newcastle over the King Edward Bridge of 1906, and a large out-of-town shopping development, the "Metro Centre",  was opened with a station on that line. The changing pattern of railway services meant that terminating trains were significantly fewer and through trains had increased. The emphasis on bay platforms at the station was no longer appropriate.
</p><p>The opportunity was taken in conjunction with the East Coast Main Line electrification scheme, inaugurated in 1991, to extend the station southwards to provide more through platforms. This encroached on to land occupied by through tracks previously used by goods trains, which had seen little use since the withdrawal of many good services in the 1960s. A new island platform was provided, built around the southern wall of the station. The two platform faces are divided so as to provide four numbered platforms, 5 to 8, generally used for local trains.<sup id="cite_ref-fawcett_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fawcett-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Station_Masters">Station Masters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Station Masters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Train_services">Train services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Train services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_Station_(geograph_3009163).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_3009163%29.jpg/220px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_3009163%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_3009163%29.jpg/330px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_3009163%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_3009163%29.jpg/440px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_3009163%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_Station_(geograph_3009163).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/East_Coast_(train_operating_company)" title="East Coast (train operating company)">East Coast</a> and <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> trains at opposite platforms</div></div></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_station,_27_July_2011_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Newcastle_Central_station%2C_27_July_2011_%282%29.jpg/220px-Newcastle_Central_station%2C_27_July_2011_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Newcastle_Central_station%2C_27_July_2011_%282%29.jpg/330px-Newcastle_Central_station%2C_27_July_2011_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Newcastle_Central_station%2C_27_July_2011_%282%29.jpg/440px-Newcastle_Central_station%2C_27_July_2011_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_station,_27_July_2011_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Departures board in the main station concourse</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_Station_(geograph_1866151).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_1866151%29.jpg/220px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_1866151%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_1866151%29.jpg/330px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_1866151%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_1866151%29.jpg/440px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%28geograph_1866151%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3396" data-file-height="2256" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_Station_(geograph_1866151).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Northern_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Rail">Northern Rail</a> services arriving/departing at Newcastle in 2010</div></div></div>
<p>Newcastle is a principal stop on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a>. The station is operated by <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="London_North_Eastern_Railway">London North Eastern Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: London North Eastern Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>London North Eastern Railway provides high-speed inter-city services southbound every half hour to London (one fast, one semi-fast) as well as 3 trains per 2 hours continue northbound into Scotland. One service is also provided each evening Monday - Friday from Newcastle to Sunderland.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>northbound to <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh Waverley</a> calling at <a href="/wiki/Berwick-upon-Tweed_railway_station" title="Berwick-upon-Tweed railway station">Berwick-upon-Tweed</a>. Extra services at peak times to Edinburgh only also call at <a href="/wiki/Morpeth_railway_station" title="Morpeth railway station">Morpeth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alnmouth_railway_station" title="Alnmouth railway station">Alnmouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dunbar_railway_station" title="Dunbar railway station">Dunbar</a>. At weekends, all daytime services arriving from London continue to Edinburgh.
<ul><li>4 services are extended daily to <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_railway_station" title="Aberdeen railway station">Aberdeen</a></li>
<li>1 service is extended daily to <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow Central</a></li>
<li>1 service is extended daily to <a href="/wiki/Inverness_railway_station" title="Inverness railway station">Inverness</a></li>
<li>1 service is extended daily to <a href="/wiki/Stirling_railway_station,_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Stirling railway station, Scotland">Stirling</a></li></ul></li>
<li>southbound to <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King's Cross</a>;
<ul><li>1 semi-fast service calling at <a href="/wiki/Durham_railway_station" title="Durham railway station">Durham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darlington_railway_station" title="Darlington railway station">Darlington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northallerton_railway_station" title="Northallerton railway station">Northallerton</a>, <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_railway_station" title="Doncaster railway station">Doncaster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newark_North_Gate_railway_station" title="Newark North Gate railway station">Newark North Gate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_railway_station" title="Peterborough railway station">Peterborough</a> and other stations on the ECML at peak times with a journey time of approximately 3 hours 20 minutes.</li>
<li>1 fast service calling at Darlington and York only with a journey time of 2 hours 50 minutes.</li>
<li>Additional services operate between Edinburgh-Newcastle/York and between Newcastle-York.</li></ul></li></ul>
<p><b>Rolling stock used:</b> <a href="/wiki/InterCity_125" title="InterCity 125">InterCity 125s</a> and <a href="/wiki/InterCity_225" title="InterCity 225">InterCity 225s</a>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flying_Scotsman">Flying Scotsman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Flying Scotsman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>early morning service, the <i><a href="/wiki/Flying_Scotsman_(train)" title="Flying Scotsman (train)">Flying Scotsman</a></i> operated by London North Eastern Railway, from Edinburgh Waverley to London King's Cross calling at Newcastle only arriving at King's Cross at 09.40, not corresponding northbound service</li></ul>
<p><b>Rolling stock used:</b> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_800" title="British Rail Class 800">Class 800s</a>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: CrossCountry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> operate services north into Scotland, supplementing London North Eastern Railway services, and southbound there are two trains per hour to the CrossCountry hub at <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham New Street</a> from where they extend towards the South West and South Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>northbound to Edinburgh Waverley hourly, continuing to Glasgow Central (every two hours) or Aberdeen (once daily) calling at most stations en route.</li>
<li>southbound to the South West of England hourly calling at Durham, Darlington, York, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Westgate_railway_station" title="Wakefield Westgate railway station">Wakefield Westgate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_railway_station" title="Chesterfield railway station">Chesterfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derby_railway_station" title="Derby railway station">Derby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burton-on-Trent_railway_station" title="Burton-on-Trent railway station">Burton-on-Trent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham New Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham_Spa_railway_station" title="Cheltenham Spa railway station">Cheltenham Spa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Parkway_railway_station" title="Bristol Parkway railway station">Bristol Parkway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Temple_Meads_railway_station" title="Bristol Temple Meads railway station">Bristol Temple Meads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exeter_St_Davids_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter St Davids railway station">Exeter St Davids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_railway_station" title="Plymouth railway station">Plymouth</a>. Three services to continue <a href="/wiki/Penzance_railway_station" title="Penzance railway station">Penzance</a>.</li>
<li>southbound to <a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">Reading</a> hourly calling at Durham, Darlington, York, Doncaster, Sheffield, Derby, Birmingham New Street, <a href="/wiki/Leamington_Spa_railway_station" title="Leamington Spa railway station">Leamington Spa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banbury_railway_station" title="Banbury railway station">Banbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oxford_railway_station" title="Oxford railway station">Oxford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">Reading</a>. Some services are continue to <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Central_railway_station" title="Southampton Central railway station">Southampton Central</a> or  <a href="/wiki/Guildford_railway_station" title="Guildford railway station">Guildford</a> (once daily).</li></ul>
<p><b>Rolling stock used:</b> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_220" title="British Rail Class 220">Class 220s</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_221" title="British Rail Class 221">Class 221s</a> and <a href="/wiki/InterCity_125" title="InterCity 125">InterCity 125s</a>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="TransPennine_Express">TransPennine Express</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: TransPennine Express">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Newcastle is a terminus for <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> services to and from  <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> via <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, some services will be extended through to Edinburgh from December 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With the electrification of the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_to_Liverpool_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester to Liverpool Line">Manchester to Liverpool Line</a>, from May 2014 a new timetable was introduced which is made up an hourly express service between Newcastle and Liverpool via Leeds and Manchester reducing journey times to Liverpool to three hours as part of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hub" title="Northern Hub">Northern Hub</a> scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Services to Leeds/York are also supplemented by London North Eastern Railway and CrossCountry.
</p>
<ul><li>southbound to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool Lime Street</a> calling at <a href="/wiki/Chester-le-Street_railway_station" title="Chester-le-Street railway station">Chester-le-Street</a>, Durham, Darlington, Northallerton, York, Leeds, <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Victoria railway station">Manchester Victoria</a>.</li>
<li>southbound to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a> calling at Durham, Darlington, Northallerton, York, Leeds, <a href="/wiki/Dewsbury_railway_station" title="Dewsbury railway station">Dewsbury</a>, Huddersfield and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a>.</li></ul>
<p><b>Rolling stock used:</b> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_185" title="British Rail Class 185">Class 185</a> diesel multiple units
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern">Northern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Northern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> operates a number of commuter and regional services&#160;:<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>northbound on the East Coast Main Line to <a href="/wiki/Cramlington_railway_station" title="Cramlington railway station">Cramlington</a> and Morpeth with services extended to <a href="/wiki/Chathill_railway_station" title="Chathill railway station">Chathill</a> at peak hours.</li>
<li>southbound along the <a href="/wiki/Durham_Coast_Line" title="Durham Coast Line">Durham Coast Line</a> to <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">Middlesbrough</a> calling at <a href="/wiki/Heworth_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Heworth railway station">Heworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunderland railway station">Sunderland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seaham_railway_station" title="Seaham railway station">Seaham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hartlepool_railway_station" title="Hartlepool railway station">Hartlepool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seaton_Carew_railway_station" title="Seaton Carew railway station">Seaton Carew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billingham_railway_station" title="Billingham railway station">Billingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockton_railway_station_(County_Durham)" title="Stockton railway station (County Durham)">Stockton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thornaby_railway_station" title="Thornaby railway station">Thornaby</a>. Extended most hours to <a href="/wiki/Nunthorpe_railway_station" title="Nunthorpe railway station">Nunthorpe</a> in order to serve the new <a href="/wiki/James_Cook_railway_station" title="James Cook railway station">railway station</a> at <a href="/wiki/James_Cook_University_Hospital" title="James Cook University Hospital">James Cook University Hospital</a> in Middlesbrough.</li>
<li>westbound on the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_Valley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyne Valley Line">Tyne Valley Line</a> to <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_railway_station" title="Carlisle railway station">Carlisle</a> calling at <a href="/wiki/MetroCentre_railway_station" title="MetroCentre railway station">MetroCentre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prudhoe_railway_station" title="Prudhoe railway station">Prudhoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hexham_railway_station" title="Hexham railway station">Hexham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haydon_Bridge_railway_station" title="Haydon Bridge railway station">Haydon Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haltwhistle_railway_station" title="Haltwhistle railway station">Haltwhistle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brampton_(Cumbria)_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Brampton (Cumbria) railway station">Brampton</a> and others at alternate hours.</li>
<li>westbound slow service on the Tyne Valley Line to Hexham calling at <a href="/wiki/Dunston_railway_station" title="Dunston railway station">Dunston</a>, MetroCentre, <a href="/wiki/Blaydon_railway_station" title="Blaydon railway station">Blaydon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wylam_railway_station" title="Wylam railway station">Wylam</a>, Prudhoe, <a href="/wiki/Stocksfield_railway_station" title="Stocksfield railway station">Stocksfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riding_Mill_railway_station" title="Riding Mill railway station">Riding Mill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corbridge_railway_station" title="Corbridge railway station">Corbridge</a> and terminating at Hexham. Extended to Carlisle at peak hours.</li>
<li>1 train per hour operates between Newcastle and Metro Centre calling at Dunston only during the day.</li></ul>
<p>Some services on the Tyne Valley line extend beyond Carlisle, including one service to <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow Central</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_South_Western_Line" title="Glasgow South Western Line">Glasgow South Western Line</a>. These services are operated using <a href="/wiki/Abellio_ScotRail" title="Abellio ScotRail">ScotRail</a> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_156" title="British Rail Class 156">Class 156s</a>, but operate as Northern services with Northern crew between Newcastle and Carlisle.
</p><p><b>Rolling stock used:</b> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_142" title="British Rail Class 142">Class 142</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_156" title="British Rail Class 156">Class 156</a> diesel multiple units
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Coast_Trains">East Coast Trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: East Coast Trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2016 ORR gave the green light to a new operator called <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Trains" title="East Coast Trains">East Coast Trains</a> which would operate services to <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh Waverley</a> via <a href="/wiki/Stevenage_railway_station" title="Stevenage railway station">Stevenage</a>, Newcastle &amp; <a href="/wiki/Morpeth_railway_station" title="Morpeth railway station">Morpeth</a>. The operation would begin operation in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RGI_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RGI-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_Northumberland_Line_to_Ashington">Proposed <i>Northumberland Line</i> to Ashington</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Proposed Northumberland Line to Ashington">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Blyth_and_Tyne_Railway#Proposed_reinstatement_of_passenger_services" title="Blyth and Tyne Railway">Blyth and Tyne Railway §&#160;Proposed reinstatement of passenger services</a></div>
<p>Since the 1990s local councils have considered the feasibility of restoring passenger services linking <a href="/wiki/Ashington" title="Ashington">Ashington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blyth,_Northumberland" title="Blyth, Northumberland">Blyth</a> with Newcastle.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBevan199859_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBevan199859-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> These early, informal, proposals suggested serving Blyth, not by reopening the branch to <a href="/wiki/Blyth_railway_station" title="Blyth railway station">Blyth station</a>, but by reopening the nearby <a href="/wiki/Newsham_railway_station" title="Newsham railway station">Newsham station</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Denis_Murphy_(UK_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Denis Murphy (UK politician)">Denis Murphy</a>, the then <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> MP for <a href="/wiki/Wansbeck_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Wansbeck (UK Parliament constituency)">Wansbeck</a>, expressed support in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Adjournment_debate" title="Adjournment debate">adjournment debate</a> in April 1999 and again in a debate in January 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>  The Railway Development Society (renamed <a href="/wiki/Railfuture" title="Railfuture">Railfuture</a> in 2000) also endorsed the proposal in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBevan199859_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBevan199859-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later, in 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Train_Operating_Companies" class="mw-redirect" title="Association of Train Operating Companies">Association of Train Operating Companies</a> published a £34 million proposal to restore passenger services from Newcastle to <a href="/wiki/Ashington_railway_station" title="Ashington railway station">Ashington</a>, serving Blyth in this way.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEATOC200917_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEATOC200917-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early 2010s, <a href="/wiki/Northumberland_County_Council" title="Northumberland County Council">Northumberland County Council (NCC)</a> became interested in the reintroduction of passenger services along the remaining freight-only section of the former <a href="/wiki/Blyth_and_Tyne_Railway" title="Blyth and Tyne Railway">Blyth and Tyne Railway</a> main line between Benton Junction and a reopened <a href="/wiki/Ashington_railway_station" title="Ashington railway station">Ashington station</a>. In June 2013 NCC commissioned <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> to complete a <a href="/wiki/Governance_for_Railway_Investment_Projects" class="mw-redirect" title="Governance for Railway Investment Projects">GRIP 1 study</a> to examine the best options for the scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The GRIP 1 study was received by NCC in March 2014 and in June 2015 they initiated a more detailed GRIP 2 Feasibility Study at a cost of £850,000.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The GRIP 2 study, which NCC received in October 2016, confirmed that the reintroduction of a frequent seven-day a week passenger service between Newcastle and Ashington was feasible and could provide economic benefits of £70 million with more than 380,000 people using the line each year by 2034.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>  This GRIP 2 study suggested construction of up to 7 new or reopened stations, potentially including a new terminus at <a href="/wiki/Woodhorn_railway_station" title="Woodhorn railway station">Woodhorn</a> (for the <a href="/wiki/Woodhorn_(Museum)" title="Woodhorn (Museum)">Woodhorn Museum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northumberland_Archives" title="Northumberland Archives">Northumberland Archives</a>) east of Ashington, with a potential end to end journey time of 37 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> At the time it was suggested that, subject to funding being raised for the £191 million<sup id="cite_ref-:0_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> scheme, detailed design work could begin in October 2018 with construction commencing four months later and the first passenger services introduced in 2021<sup id="cite_ref-:0_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> though by October 2018 such works were yet to begin.
</p><p>After receiving the GRIP 2 study, NCC initially announced that they were preceding with a GRIP 3 Study from Network Rail but such a report was not commissioned at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Despite a change in the political leadership of Northumberland County Council following the <a href="/wiki/2017_Northumberland_County_Council_election" title="2017 Northumberland County Council election">2017 local elections</a><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> the authority continued to work towards the reintroduction of a passenger service onto the line,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> encouraged by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport's</a> November 2017 report, <i>A Strategic Vision for Rail</i>, which named the line as a possible candidate for a future reintroduction of passenger services.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Consequentially, NCC commissioned a further interim study in November 2017 (dubbed <i>GRIP 2B</i>) to determine whether high costs and long timescales identified in the GRIP 2 Study could be reduced by reducing the initial scope of the project but the report failed to deliver on this.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Northumberland County Council has, however, continued to develop the project, announcing an additional £3.46 million in funding for a further business case and detailed design study<sup id="cite_ref-:2_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> (equivalent to GRIP 3)<sup id="cite_ref-:1_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> to be completed by the end of 2019, with the first passenger services potentially being introduced on the line in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> However, the revised proposals, released in July 2019, are reduced in scope from the plan considered in the 2016 GRIP 2 study and propose 4-phase project<sup id="cite_ref-:4_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> to reduce the initial cost of the scheme. As such, the initial phase, at an estimated £90 million,<sup id="cite_ref-:2_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> would see the creation of new or reopened National Rail stations at only <b><a href="/wiki/Northumberland_Park_Metro_station" title="Northumberland Park Metro station">Northumberland Park</a></b>, <b>Newsham</b>, <b><a href="/wiki/Bedlington_railway_station" title="Bedlington railway station">Bedlington</a></b> and <b>Ashington</b> as well as a number of other infrastructure upgrades.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Two further stations, at <b><a href="/wiki/Seaton_Delaval_railway_station" title="Seaton Delaval railway station">Seaton Delaval</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Bebside_railway_station#Reopening_proposals" title="Bebside railway station">Blyth Bebside</a></b> and further infrastructure upgrades would then follow in later phases.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The previously proposed station at Woodhorn appears to have been dropped from the scheme entirely.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/North_East_Joint_Transport_Committee" title="North East Joint Transport Committee">North East Joint Transport Committee's</a> bid for the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">UK Government's</a> Transfroming Cities Fund, submitted on 20 June 2019, includes £99 million to fund the first phase of the Newcastle to Ashington <i>Northumberland Line</i> project,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> while further work is ongoing to secure additional public and private investment.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Layout_and_platforms">Layout and platforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Layout and platforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_railway_station.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Newcastle_railway_station.JPG/220px-Newcastle_railway_station.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Newcastle_railway_station.JPG/330px-Newcastle_railway_station.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Newcastle_railway_station.JPG/440px-Newcastle_railway_station.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_railway_station.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Departures board between platforms 3 and 4</div></div></div>
<p>The National Rail station has 12 platforms. The arrangement is:
</p>
<ul><li>Platform 1 is an east-facing bay platform which handles terminating Northern local services from the south over the <a href="/wiki/High_Level_Bridge" title="High Level Bridge">High Level Bridge</a> and from the north.</li>
<li>Platform 2 is the main through platform for London North Eastern Railway and CrossCountry services heading northbound to Scotland.</li>
<li>Platforms 3 and 4 are the main through platforms for southbound London North Eastern Railway services to London and for southbound CrossCountry services to Birmingham and the southwest. They are also used for inter-city services which terminate at Newcastle including London North Eastern Railway services from London, evening London North Eastern Railway services from Edinburgh, and some cCrossCountry services. Some northbound trains also stop here.</li>
<li>Platforms 5/6 share the northbound side, and Platforms 7/8 the southbound side, of the newer island platform, and are used mainly by Northern services westbound to Hexham and Carlisle and eastbound to Sunderland and Middlesbrough.</li>
<li>Platforms 9 to 12 are west-facing bay terminal platforms. Platforms 9 and 10 are used for TransPennine Express services heading to Manchester and Liverpool and some Northern Rail Tyne Valley trains. CrossCountry services heading to Reading via Doncaster mainly use platform 11. Platform 12 is mainly used by CrossCountry trains for termination and some departures.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Station_redevelopment">Station redevelopment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Station redevelopment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_Newcastle_Railway_Station_(geograph_3609299).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Entrance_to_Newcastle_Railway_Station_%28geograph_3609299%29.jpg/220px-Entrance_to_Newcastle_Railway_Station_%28geograph_3609299%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Entrance_to_Newcastle_Railway_Station_%28geograph_3609299%29.jpg/330px-Entrance_to_Newcastle_Railway_Station_%28geograph_3609299%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Entrance_to_Newcastle_Railway_Station_%28geograph_3609299%29.jpg/440px-Entrance_to_Newcastle_Railway_Station_%28geograph_3609299%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_Newcastle_Railway_Station_(geograph_3609299).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Station redevelopment underway at entrance to Newcastle Central Station</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_Station_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Newcastle_Central_Station_%282%29.jpg/220px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Newcastle_Central_Station_%282%29.jpg/330px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Newcastle_Central_Station_%282%29.jpg/440px-Newcastle_Central_Station_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1526" data-file-height="1053" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_Central_Station_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A British Rail InterCity service at Newcastle in 1983</div></div></div>
<p>Plans were revealed on 30 April 2013 for a major redevelopment,<sup id="cite_ref-exciting_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exciting-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> including an £8.6 million project to regenerate the inside of the station,<sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and a further £11.4 million to develop the area surrounding the station.<sup id="cite_ref-revamping_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revamping-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The portico redevelopment was completed in April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Portico2014_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portico2014-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The redevelopment plans contain a number of improvements, including:
</p>
<ul><li>New retail space in the portico area, which will be turned into glazed arches to provide weather protection as well as retail units replacing the existing ticket office and travel centre. This will double the current amount of retail space to make it equivalent to that of the new <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">King's Cross Station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-exciting_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exciting-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chronicle20130312_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle20130312-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tobenefit_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tobenefit-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The travel centre and ticket office will be reduced in size and relocated to the area beyond where the current <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s_Local" title="Sainsbury&#39;s Local">Sainsbury's Local store</a> is.<sup id="cite_ref-exciting_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exciting-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chronicle20130311_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle20130311-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Improved toilet facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-exciting_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exciting-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tobenefit_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tobenefit-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Clearer signage.<sup id="cite_ref-exciting_48-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exciting-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tobenefit_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tobenefit-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Increased covered cycle-park space.<sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>A simpler layout that accentuates the grade one listed architecture including the <a href="/wiki/The_Castle,_Newcastle" title="The Castle, Newcastle">Castle Keep</a>. The line of sight across the concourse will also be greatly improved.<sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Sand-blasting of the walls and new lighting to be fitted.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle20130311_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle20130311-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The current access points to the station will be moved to make it easier to enter and leave the station.<sup id="cite_ref-exciting_48-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exciting-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Improved waiting rooms.<sup id="cite_ref-tobenefit_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tobenefit-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Alteration to the existing bridge structure.<sup id="cite_ref-tobenefit_53-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tobenefit-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>New lifts and escalators.<sup id="cite_ref-tobenefit_53-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tobenefit-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>New glazed canopies.<sup id="cite_ref-tobenefit_53-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tobenefit-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The redevelopment plan also includes a number of improvements to the area surrounding the station, including:
</p>
<ul><li>New taxi rank to the east side of the portico.<sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chronicle20130312_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle20130312-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chronicle20130311_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle20130311-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>A two-way cycle track at the west end of Neville Street.<sup id="cite_ref-exciting_48-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exciting-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chronicle20130311_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle20130311-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Change of traffic flow patterns to ease congestion.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Pedestrian crossings on Neville Street and Grainger Street.<sup id="cite_ref-exciting_48-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exciting-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Pedestrianisation of the car-park space outside the Centurion Pub.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle20130312_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle20130312-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chronicle20130311_54-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle20130311-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Wider footways and pavement cafes outside the station.<sup id="cite_ref-exciting_48-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exciting-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The work began in May 2013 and was completed during April 2014 by Miller Construction.<sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The station operated as normal throughout the works.<sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The £8.6 million funding for the internal station work was provided by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a>'s Station Commercial Project Facility Fund.<sup id="cite_ref-newera_49-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newera-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The external works were jointly funded by NE1, Regional Growth Fund and <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_City_Council" title="Newcastle City Council">Newcastle City Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-revamping_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revamping-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway_infrastructure">Railway infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Railway infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r910949775">.mw-parser-output .RMbox{box-shadow:0 2px 2px 0 rgba(0,0,0,.14),0 1px 5px 0 rgba(0,0,0,.12),0 3px 1px -2px rgba(0,0,0,.2)}.mw-parser-output
