</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Trains cross the <a href="/wiki/River_Tyne" title="River Tyne">River Tyne</a> on one of two bridges.  The older <a href="/wiki/High_Level_Bridge" title="High Level Bridge">High Level Bridge</a> south-east of the station, designed by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stephenson" title="Robert Stephenson">Robert Stephenson</a> opened on 27 September 1849.  Its location meant north-south trains had to reverse in the station to continue their journey.  The <a href="/wiki/King_Edward_VII_Bridge" title="King Edward VII Bridge">King Edward VII Bridge</a> south-west of the station opened on 10 July 1906 allowing north-south trains to continue without reversing. The two bridges enable the <a href="/wiki/Rail_tracks" class="mw-redirect" title="Rail tracks">trackwork</a> north and south of the river to form a complete circle, allowing trains to be turned if necessary. The former <a href="/wiki/Gateshead_TMD" title="Gateshead TMD">Gateshead depot</a>, next to the connecting tracks on the south side of the Tyne, mirrored Newcastle station.
</p><p>The station was noted for its complex set of <a href="/wiki/Level_junction" title="Level junction">diamond crossings</a> to the east of the station which facilitated access to the High Level Bridge and northbound East Coast Main Line and was said to be the greatest such crossing in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
The crossing was the subject of many early-1900s post cards, titled <i>The Largest Railway Crossing in the World</i> - photographed from the castle (towards the station), or from the station towards the castle.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The crossing has been simplified in recent years as the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear_Metro" title="Tyne and Wear Metro">Metro</a> brought about the withdrawal of many heavy-rail suburban services and the closure of the bay platforms they operated from on the north side of the station removing the need for such a complex crossing.  Much of this work was carried out in 1988-9 as part of remodelling and resignalling work associated with ECML electrification.  A new island platform on the former goods lines was commissioned as part of this work, with signalling control relocated to the Tyneside IECC on the opposite side of the river. <a href="/wiki/Heaton_TMD" title="Heaton TMD">Heaton depot</a> is to the north of the station, on the East Coast Main Line.
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>On 17 August 1951, two <a href="/wiki/Electric_multiple_unit" title="Electric multiple unit">electric multiple units</a> were in a head-on collision after one of them departed against a danger signal. Two people were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoole4_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoole4-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On 19 April 1955, a collision occurred between <a href="/wiki/LNER_Class_V2" title="LNER Class V2">V2</a> locomotive 60968 and <a href="/wiki/LMS_Fairburn_2-6-4T" title="LMS Fairburn 2-6-4T">Fairburn tank</a> locomotive No. 42085 on the diamond crossings. Both locomotives were derailed.<sup id="cite_ref-Trevena2_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trevena2-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span id="Tyne_.26_Wear_Metro"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tyne_&amp;_Wear_Metro">Tyne &amp; Wear Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tyne &amp; Wear Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Central_Station_Metro_station" title="Central Station Metro station">Central Station Metro station</a></div>
<p>Newcastle station is located above Central metro station on the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear_Metro" title="Tyne and Wear Metro">Tyne and Wear Metro</a>, one of five underground stations serving the city centre. Central is an interchange between the Yellow and Green lines, and is the last stop prior to crossing the <a href="/wiki/River_Tyne" title="River Tyne">River Tyne</a> towards <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a>.
</p>
